<div id="review_426155958" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/426155958" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1801139-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442883443p2/1801139.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/426155958?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/1801139-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1801139-sarah?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1801139-sarah?shelf=slice-of-life">slice-of-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1801139-sarah?shelf=lols">lols</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer426155958&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer426155958" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17827219238003676665"><br/>While I myself am not much of a fan of this pink and flowery genre (or sub-genre?) called "chick-lit," I would have to say I enjoyed some books in this category. I very much prefer reading dystopian novels or some intensely psychological/twisted books over reading the womanly woes of teenage drama queens, but I guess one can never be truly faithful; I sometimes needed breaks from death, murder, gloom and overall psycho-ness. And when I needed those breaks, chick-lit books would be there at some </span>
  <span id="freeText17827219238003676665" style="display:none"><br />While I myself am not much of a fan of this pink and flowery genre (or sub-genre?) called "chick-lit," I would have to say I enjoyed some books in this category. I very much prefer reading dystopian novels or some intensely psychological/twisted books over reading the womanly woes of teenage drama queens, but I guess one can never be truly faithful; I sometimes needed breaks from death, murder, gloom and overall psycho-ness. And when I needed those breaks, chick-lit books would be there at some hidden corners of my bookshelf, waiting to be opened, a hidden but never forgotten mistress. Kind of like a guilty pleasure. So I guess, in a way, I'm also kind of a fan of chick-lit. However, this book, The Lonely Hearts Club, disappointed me. I think this is a lot, coming from someone who's capable of loving every book she encounters. I loved How To Date Like A Guy (by Clarksley). I enjoyed You Wish (by Hubbard). I adored Flipped (by Van Draanen), and I absolutely gorged on the feast that is The Karma Club (by Brody). I even liked the Twilight saga (by Meyer), for the simple reason that it gets kids started on their reading habits.<br /><br />I stumbled upon The Lonely Hearts Club while I was reading reviews of The Karma Club, actually. Some reviewers said that TLHC was similar to TKC, so being the book glutton that I am, I ended up reading it.<br /><br />So, about this book called The Lonely Hearts Club...<br /><br />I didn't really like Penny, the protagonist. I mean, except for the fact that she has a lame name (she said so herself), she didn't show much character development throughout the story. At the end of the book, she was still every bit the inconsiderate, self-absorbed girl that she was at the beginning. I am now going to confess that I finished this book more for Diane than for Penny. Diane's a jewel. She defied odds, went against society, went against the image of her faux-self, and recreated her sense of self. She went for new goals. She's sweet, was pretty much the backbone of the story, and was the most awesome character. I had wasted days wondering why she wasn't the main character of this book.<br /><br />But back to Penny Lane Bloom.<br /><br />Since the book was Penny-centric, I guess I just wasn't able to ignore her flaws. She was using the club as an excuse to withdraw to her own shell and just give up on Ryan Bauer. I didn't like how her friends (mostly DIANE) did everything for her. I know you might think I'm bashing Penny, but really, I'm not. Honestly, I hated Missy for being such a bitch. <br /><br />Penny was pretty smart to come up with something like the club. And she had a cool sense of style. So she's stylish, smart, not afraid to just say "fuck it all", and had a rocking body. She had a lot in her to be admired. But I just can't help but think that a lot of her good points were, if you would notice, purely aesthetic. ..... And she just <i>had</i> to be insecure. I mean, I get that at the beginning protagonists have to be insecure, or maybe at some point in the middle of the story, but Penny Lane Bloom was an insecure and paranoid girl throughout the book. Or at least until the part where she asked Ryan out, which was wholly due to Tracy's and Diane's efforts. And that was like, what, at the last page?<br /><br />Sigh.<br /><br />Now that I think about it, maybe Penny's okay. I mean, if you're pretty, smart, fit and stylish, you can't possibly have the perfect personality too, right? That makes Penny real. I just wish Penny had a backbone. And not just in those last few pages, but on other parts of the book as well. She would have made an awesome ass-kicker. <br /><br />Oh well. I guess you can't have everything.<br /><br />Poor Ryan Bauer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17827219238003676665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_321174824" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321174824" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581282691p2/5501124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321174824?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Amanda by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1154815-estelle">Estelle</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321174824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10039878570904475440">Penny Lane Bloom is the daughter of Beatles fanatics. Her parents named her after the song Penny Lane and her sisters are named Rita and Lucy after the songs Lovely Rita and Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds. Every summer her family spends their holidays with close family friends, the Taylors, including their son Nate. Nate and Penny Lane have been best friends since they were little kids and their feelings for each other grow stronger as they age. Unfortunately things don't go as well as Penny has </span>
  <span id="freeText10039878570904475440" style="display:none">Penny Lane Bloom is the daughter of Beatles fanatics. Her parents named her after the song Penny Lane and her sisters are named Rita and Lucy after the songs Lovely Rita and Lucy in the Sky with Diamonds. Every summer her family spends their holidays with close family friends, the Taylors, including their son Nate. Nate and Penny Lane have been best friends since they were little kids and their feelings for each other grow stronger as they age. Unfortunately things don't go as well as Penny has always dreamed and she decides she will no longer date boys. Inspired by her favourite band, The Beatles, she starts The Lonely Hearts Club.<br /><br />At first she's the only member but soon the number of club members grows but not everyone is impressed with the club and their goals. And then Penny realises there is a boy she likes but how can she date him with her club depending on her?<br /><br />Unfortunately this club means that Penny seems really anti-boys and the club starts to annoy her male classmates. It also doesn't help when Ryan starts being really nice to her and asking her out on dates. Penny won't even admit to herself that she has feelings for Ryan. I could really tell that Penny struggled with this. <br /><br />The Lonely Hearts Club by Elizabeth Eulberg was a very fun read. Each part features the title of a Beatles song that fits what's going on in Penny's life at the time and there are lots of Beatles references and song lyrics throughout the story.<br /><br />Penny was immediately likeable and I really felt for her when her dream boy let her down. The Beatles, on the other hand, have always been there for her. She's always loved their music and even though some teens might rebel against the musical tastes of their parents like, she hasn't. Her parents are total Beatles fans, they're vegetarian because Paul McCartney is, their door bell rings to the tune of Love Me Do and they detest cover bands. <br /><br />Her best friend Tracey was not supportive of the club at first as she's always trying to find a boy to date but she eventually comes around, as does Penny's previous best friend, Diane. Diane cut her out of her life the moment she started dating Ryan, four years ago. Penny was hurt by Diane's actions and wouldn't want to go through that again and that's part of why she wants this club to work, she wants girls to be there for each other instead of ditching their friends as soon as they get a boyfriend. I really liked this idea that girls should help each other out instead of bitching and backstabbing and thought Penny was clever to think of a way to unite her classmates.<br /><br />There were times I thought things would be very predictable but sometimes I was pleasantly surprised when a scene didn't go how I thought it would and the ending was really sweet and a great conclusion to this story. Also, this book made me really nostalgic as I went through a Beatles phase when I was a teen, my mum loved to tell people that I had Beatlemania, and I could totally understand Penny's love for the band.<br /><br />The Lonely Hearts Club would be a fantastic read for fans of realistic fiction and cute YA love stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10039878570904475440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132587634" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132587634" />
    <a title="Katya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4324634-katya"><img alt="Katya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285183076p2/4324634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132587634?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katya" href="/user/show/4324634-katya">Katya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132587634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6312495493858758428">It's been a while since I read a book in one sitting. I'd forgotten what it was like, to completely immerse yourself into it and fall just a little bit in love.<br/><br/>Penny Lane is just your typical teenager... well, if you don't count her parents' religious obsession with the Beatles. Oddly enough, I can relate to that particular aspect, being an ABBA kid myself. When she finds her childhood friend turned boyfriend with another girl, though, she decides to rethink her position on dating and boys, and </span>
  <span id="freeText6312495493858758428" style="display:none">It's been a while since I read a book in one sitting. I'd forgotten what it was like, to completely immerse yourself into it and fall just a little bit in love.<br /><br />Penny Lane is just your typical teenager... well, if you don't count her parents' religious obsession with the Beatles. Oddly enough, I can relate to that particular aspect, being an ABBA kid myself. When she finds her childhood friend turned boyfriend with another girl, though, she decides to rethink her position on dating and boys, and decides to give it up for the next two years. Thus, the Lonely Hearts Club is born, and as it slowly gains popularity, Penny begins to realize she has more going on than just a ban on boys.<br /><br />What I love, love, loved about this book is probably how friendship is slowly being rediscovered throughout the girls' experiences. I know it sounds cheesy and dramatic, but in a literature where friendships are highly unlikely due to the fact that they will not do good in the Stockholm Syndrome relationships that substitute 'love' (no example needed), it's very rare to see a book which highlights the fact that above love, girls need their friends' support to get along. <br /><br />Penny is charming. She's sweet, she's quirky, she's naturally embarrassed by her parents, and she's a little bit too intense (but try finding a teenager that isn't). Some might argue that she becomes annoying when she turns into this semi-Christ figure for the jilted girls in school, or that she stresses over it too much, but in my opinion, it was very realistically portrayed. It took me back a few years, when no word spoken didn't inflict some damage, when no action went unnoticed and unscrutinized, if not by the peers, than by myself. It was refreshing, and I loved the book for it.<br /><br />Also:<br /><br />I loved how important issues were brought up without hitting the reader across the head with a Bible.<br /><br />I loved how girls discovered that it was not a boyfriendless life they needed, but a supportive group of friends.<br /><br />I loved how boyfriends could make it into that group.<br /><br />But most of all...<br /><br />I loved the walrus!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6312495493858758428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_227622742" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227622742" />
    <a title="Tammi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6274976-tammi"><img alt="Tammi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319578400p2/6274976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227622742?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammi" href="/user/show/6274976-tammi">Tammi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227622742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16059886031789003099">You know how the term ‘feel-good’ is applied to certain movies? I don’t know how often it’s used to describe books, but if any book were to fit the definition, it would be The Lonely Hearts Club. This is totally a feel-good book. I had a smile on my face almost the entire time I was reading it, laughed out loud in a few places and may have even punched the air once or twice. Mostly because of the… <br/><br/>Female empowerment and solidarity! Woo-hoo! It was so great to read a book that promotes and celebr</span>
  <span id="freeText16059886031789003099" style="display:none">You know how the term ‘feel-good’ is applied to certain movies? I don’t know how often it’s used to describe books, but if any book were to fit the definition, it would be The Lonely Hearts Club. This is totally a feel-good book. I had a smile on my face almost the entire time I was reading it, laughed out loud in a few places and may have even punched the air once or twice. Mostly because of the… <br /><br />Female empowerment and solidarity! Woo-hoo! It was so great to read a book that promotes and celebrates female friendship. It perfectly captures why girls standing up together, girls sticking up for each other, girls encouraging each other and girls just hanging out and having fun together is one of the best things in the world. This book should be handed to every female who dismisses girlfriends and claims to prefer the company of men. Because they know not what they are missing.<br /><br />Penny’s a fab heroine and I especially liked her when she was telling arseholes off. Penny’s dad, to borrow a phrase from Eulberg herself, was ‘adorbs’.<br /><br />However, while I’m not trying to single out Eulberg for this - it’s just a disappointing thing about mainstream YA in general - in so many stories everybody is white, middle-class and heterosexual. I understand that is the experience of life for some people and that's fine, but it would just be nice to see all different types of people get included. I thought it would have fit in here if one girl in the Club had come to the conclusion that dating boys actually wasn’t for her at all and would probably never be. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16059886031789003099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_423039477" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423039477" />
    <a title="Mansi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12036486-mansi"><img alt="Mansi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354012141p2/12036486.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/423039477?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mansi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mansi" href="/user/show/12036486-mansi">Mansi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12036486-mansi?shelf=very-well-written">very-well-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12036486-mansi?shelf=laugh-out-loud-funny">laugh-out-loud-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12036486-mansi?shelf=good-young-adult">good-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12036486-mansi?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423039477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7024998943938412025">- Have you ever had a disastrous almost relationship?<br/>- Do you have resentful feelings towards boys?<br/>- Are you looking to feel empowered by inspirational women?<br/><br/>Then this book is for you!<br/><br/>A light, pretty predictable read - bonus points for the creative idea and wit, though. <br/><br/>Angry and heartbroken Penny Lane swears off boys and starts 'The Lonely Hearts Club' (she's a Beatles fan) after her sort-of childhood boyfriend Nate pressures her for sex and cheats on her. Her best friends and a many other boy-</span>
  <span id="freeText7024998943938412025" style="display:none">- Have you ever had a disastrous almost relationship?<br />- Do you have resentful feelings towards boys?<br />- Are you looking to feel empowered by inspirational women?<br /><br />Then this book is for you!<br /><br />A light, pretty predictable read - bonus points for the creative idea and wit, though. <br /><br />Angry and heartbroken Penny Lane swears off boys and starts 'The Lonely Hearts Club' (she's a Beatles fan) after her sort-of childhood boyfriend Nate pressures her for sex and cheats on her. Her best friends and a many other boy-bitter peers join the club and they organise weekly meetings. Gradually, the club is a hit and there are over fifty members, all girls.<br /><br />The male population at school either don't take the club seriously or:<br />- Think they're playing hard-to-get<br />- Think they're lesbians/hardcore feminists.<br />Except for totally cute popular jock, Ryan, who has a crush on Penny, and vice versa. This creates a predicament as The Lonely Hearts' members are forbidden to date. What will Penny, the club's founder and leader do?<br /><br />Enter Todd, Ryan's best friend, who has a thing for Penny, and Nate, who pleads forgiveness furthur down the book's storyline. <br /><br />Penny Lane is sassy, funny and brave and one of the only female protagonists I don't hate. However, she does take the boy-hate to extremes sometimes. Also, I LOVE HER PARENTS! The best book parents - like, ever.<br /><br />Overall, every charater in this book is a cliche, and the plot is highly unoriginal, aside for 'The Lonely Hearts Club' concept. <br /><br />A quick, humorous read!</span>

<div id="review_152101758" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152101758" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/981388-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290055198p2/981388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152101758?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/981388-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152101758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7755273071047831800">Most of the time these "High School" genre books blur into one big mass of lip gloss and "whatevers." This one, stands apart....a little. There is at least an attempt to depart from the usual plot, although, you do end up at the same place as all the others. What I thought was interesting about this one was my realization from it. That I truly am a social misfit. In the beginning, as Penny is swearing off men for good, and glorifying in the simplicity of her new life, I found myself nodding my h</span>
  <span id="freeText7755273071047831800" style="display:none">Most of the time these "High School" genre books blur into one big mass of lip gloss and "whatevers." This one, stands apart....a little. There is at least an attempt to depart from the usual plot, although, you do end up at the same place as all the others. What I thought was interesting about this one was my realization from it. That I truly am a social misfit. In the beginning, as Penny is swearing off men for good, and glorifying in the simplicity of her new life, I found myself nodding my head in heartfelt agreement. Then as her life became increasingly complicated by interweaving her life with the females she surrounded herself with, I found myself taken aback in wonder, disgust and fear. Never, in my worst nightmere, would I chose to interconnect my life to that degree. As a child/teenager I dreamed of the day I would live naked. On a mountain. Alone. I still fantasize about such an arrangement (despite my WONDERFUL husband four INCREDIBLE children). So despite the predictability and shallow nature of the book, I enjoyed the easy read as well as the evaluation of my inner psyche.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7755273071047831800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2758703262&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2758703262" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11265945485359266933">I picked up this book, be because the book sounded really good. I thought it would be about girls who learn to find themselves before finding their soul mates. But the actual book isn't good. <br/><br/>Throughout the book, you get r/imnotlikeothergirls, r/nicegirls, and r/thathappened vibes. Penny sees all men as scums and they only date girls to get with them and break their hearts. She also sees other girls who don't agree with her views as stuck up and bratty. <br/><br/>I also think Penny failed to understand th</span>
  <span id="freeText11265945485359266933" style="display:none">I picked up this book, be because the book sounded really good. I thought it would be about girls who learn to find themselves before finding their soul mates. But the actual book isn't good. <br /><br />Throughout the book, you get r/imnotlikeothergirls, r/nicegirls, and r/thathappened vibes. Penny sees all men as scums and they only date girls to get with them and break their hearts. She also sees other girls who don't agree with her views as stuck up and bratty. <br /><br />I also think Penny failed to understand that it is high school. You don't usually find your soulmate in high school. While some guys were rude and inconsiderate, other guys weren't at all. <br /><br />The only thing I liked was when it ended. The girls did eventually learn that not all men are terrible or players. But as they say, it's not about the destination it is about the journey and the journey wasn't fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11265945485359266933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_19071270'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19071270-puedo-so-ar-contigo"><img alt="¿Puedo soñar contigo? (El club de los incomprendidos, #3)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1385843446l/19071270._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xmZH1HL71QF7tX7kdY7BLwXzWXZxXNlEg8pmvEZXlH0XtPfDQWPV2ZqogHLo9UuICZj1ybhDbYkKvrUF/ugh5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

  <span id="freeText1799973399454605573" style="display:none">The short and sweet version:<br />Elizabeth Eulberg was born and raised in Wisconsin before heading off to college at Syracuse University and making a career in the New York City book biz. Now a full-time writer, she is the author of The Lonely Hearts Club, Prom &amp; Prejudice, Take a Bow, Revenge of the Girl with the Great Personality, Better Off Friends, We Can Work it Out, Just Another Girl, Past Perfect Life, and The Great Shelby Holmes series. She lives outside of Manhattan with her three guitars, two keyboards, and one drumstick.<br /><br />To check out the long version, head over to my webpage: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.elizabetheulberg.com/bio/">http://www.elizabetheulberg.com/bio/</a><br /><br />Also, I'm not checking e-mails on my Goodreads, see my website for information on contacting me! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.elizabetheulberg.com/faq/">http://www.elizabetheulberg.com/faq/</a><br /><br />Happy reading!</span>
